  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_91b572b1-1a13-41e6-ab1a-d027c13b0425'
      });
    }

  <span id="freeText17577073821414444593" style="display:none"><i>In the Ichidian Universe, The League and their ruthless assassins rule all. Expertly trained and highly valued, the League Assassins are the backbone of the government. But not even the League is immune to corruption . . .</i><br /><br />Command Assassin Nykyrian Quikiades once turned his back on the League—and has been hunted by them ever since. Though many have tried, none can kill him or stop him from completing his current mission: to protect Kiara Zamir, a woman whose father’s political alliance has made her a target. <br /><br />As her world becomes even deadlier, Kiara must entrust her life to the same kind of beast who once killed her mother and left her for dead. Old enemies and new threaten them both and the only way they can survive is to overcome their suspicions and learn to trust in the very ones who threaten them the most: each other.</span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7945849740836123348"><b>4 Stars</b><br/><br/>What up, what up, what up my friends.<br/><br/>How was everyone's holiday? <br/><br/>Mine was swell. I spent Christmas Eve spreading holiday cheer...<br/><br/>AKA champagne...<br/><br/>But what can I say. <br/><br/> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1482984146i/21568710._SY540_.jpg' width='225' height='315' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>And Christmas Eve hung the fuck over from all the champagne.<br/><br/>Whoops. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1482984551i/21568730._SY540_.jpg' width='282' height='376' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Let's just say I never realized how loud the ripping of wrapping paper sounded. <br/><br/>But I digress. <br/><br/>This book. <br/><br/>I deliberated over my rating on this for a bit. <br/><br/>I was really enjoying everything and then there were a few too many "convenient" twists toward the end fo</span>
  <span id="freeText7945849740836123348" style="display:none"><b>4 Stars</b><br><br>What up, what up, what up my friends.<br><br>How was everyone's holiday? <br><br>Mine was swell. I spent Christmas Eve spreading holiday cheer...<br><br>AKA champagne...<br><br>But what can I say. <br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1482984146i/21568710._SY540_.jpg" width="225" height="315" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And Christmas Eve hung the fuck over from all the champagne.<br><br>Whoops. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1482984551i/21568730._SY540_.jpg" width="282" height="376" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Let's just say I never realized how loud the ripping of wrapping paper sounded. <br><br>But I digress. <br><br>This book. <br><br>I deliberated over my rating on this for a bit. <br><br>I was really enjoying everything and then there were a few too many "convenient" twists toward the end for my liking. <br><br>But after further deliberation, I came to the conclusion...<br><br><br>Who the fuck cares. <br><br>As a PNR WHORE, I have some serious appreciation for world building done right. <br><br>And this book had that in spades. So for that alone it deserves a good rating. <br><br>I also really liked the hero.<br><br>The heroine...not as much. <br><br>But we can't always have everything, I guess. <br><br>Find me at:<br><br><a href="https://www.facebook.com/SteamyReadsBlog/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_572217433" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/572217433" />
    <a title="Nathaniel Hardman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1606092-nathaniel-hardman"><img alt="Nathaniel Hardman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1241453679p2/1606092.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/572217433?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nathaniel Hardman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nathaniel Hardman" href="/user/show/1606092-nathaniel-hardman">Nathaniel Hardman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 0759550212" href="/book/show/476692.Born_of_the_Night">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer572217433" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2756148782423665974">Here are some taglines that would be really great to put on the back cover of this book:<br/><br/>"Troubled ex-assassin Nykyrian takes on his most difficult assignment ever - to protect the Princess Kiara from the universe's most deadly killers. But when things turn personal, Nykyrian finds that saving Kiara may mean facing the one enemy he fears most of all - love."<br/><br/>Or: "Like Twilight, but dumber and dirtier!"<br/><br/>Maybe I should say first that this was a new genre for me. One time I wrote <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/331122182' rel='nofollow noopener'>a negative review</a> of </span>
  <span id="freeText2756148782423665974" style="display:none">Here are some taglines that would be really great to put on the back cover of this book:<br /><br />"Troubled ex-assassin Nykyrian takes on his most difficult assignment ever - to protect the Princess Kiara from the universe's most deadly killers. But when things turn personal, Nykyrian finds that saving Kiara may mean facing the one enemy he fears most of all - love."<br /><br />Or: "Like Twilight, but dumber and dirtier!"<br /><br />Maybe I should say first that this was a new genre for me. One time I wrote <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/331122182" rel="nofollow noopener">a negative review</a> of a book based on the Dungeons and Dragons board game, and I got some disgruntled feedback that I was really complaining about the genre and not the book. That may be the case here. Maybe space-sleaze just isn't for me. But I am astounded to see the average rating for this book. 4.24!? That's higher than <i>Huckleberry Finn</i>! Or <i>To Kill a Mockingbird</i>! Or <i>A Tale of Two Cities</i>. And those are like, REAL BOOKS. Anyway, I don't get it, and maybe I should leave it at that. <br /><br />But I won't! <br /><br />First, for a book about "deadly assassins", they sure don't seem very deadly. So this is the distant future (To illustrate how distant, they are always climbing in their "transports" or "fighters" and touching down on other planets just a few minutes later. There's absolutely no sense of space or time. Anyway, far distant future). And the bad guys want the princess dead at any cost. So the princess takes her bodyguards with her to a party (?), and rather than just shoot her from a distance, the deadly assassin comes up behind her in the bustling crowd, sticks a gun in her ribs, and tells her to walk with him out of the room. Then they get out of the party, and he throws her on the ground, and he decides to deliver a little monologue to her before shooting her (But what do you think? Does he finish and kill her before her bodyguard saves her? I won't spoil anything). Deadly assassins! <br /><br />And romance! The hero in this book is just so hot! And mysterious and aloof! And he's a gourmet chef! He always wears shades to hide his eyes because he says that people always get uncomfortable when they see his eyes. But what do they look like? Did he inherit the red eyes of his Anderian mother? Or some freakish anomaly from being a half-breed? Nope. They're just normal green eyes. But they're really beautiful! And they expose a sensitive, fragile, wounded soul. I almost wept when I read about that, it was just so darn tender. Romance! Deadly assassins! <br /><br />A couple of days after the party incident, the princess goes on a little date with her bodyguard/love-interest. They buy clothes! And ice cream! And eat at a really great restaurant! And he can totally buy her, like, THE NICEST THINGS!!!! So hot. Incidentally, did you know that in the real world, <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Longest_recorded_sniper_kills" rel="nofollow noopener">the longest confirmed sniper kill</a> was over 1.5 miles? How far might trained, deadly assassins shoot in the future? That is a question that Sherrilyn Kenyon spent a lot of time not asking herself while writing this book.<br /><br />Also, I just have to mention this because it's hilarious - at one point, our heroine is in the house of our hero-with-a-dark-secretive-past, and she's looking through his movie collection, and she finds a box labeled private (!). She puts in those movies, and - I AM NOT MAKING THIS UP! - they're a history of his life in little vignettes. She sees him as a little boy, being horribly abused in an orphanage. She sees him at school defending a smaller boy from bullies and being beaten in return. She sees him coming home from prison (he was framed!) and being beaten by his foster father. She sees him being rejected by his first lover. She sees him in a dark alley where he's been badly wounded, and he's saved by the younger version of his current best friend. It's very touching and sad, and I bet she was glad that someone had taken the time to get all of these scenes on video so she could understand the troubled past of our brooding, beautiful hero. And how do you think this scene ends? Do you think our hero might show up while she's watching these private movies and be furious with her for invading his privacy? You'll have to find out for yourself! I won't spoil anything!<br /><br />And then, holy cow does this turn into the craziest soap opera you've ever imagined. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[So they travel to this distant planet in the middle of nowhere, and the hero goes to talk to the wife of his arch nemesis - the guy who's trying to kill our heroine. And it turns out that the arch-nemesis's wife once slept with our hero, and our hero has a teenage daughter who has been raised by his arch-nemesis! Then they leave that house, and they're walking down the street, and they happen to walk past the hero's long-lost, half-crazy mother who recognizes him from when he was a four-year-old boy (he's now in his 30's). And it turns out he's actually the crown prince of the Anderians, but his grandmother hated him for being half-human, so she sent him to a human orphanage and faked his death so his family wouldn't look for him. And it turns out that the woman our hero remembers who threw him cruelly into the orphanage was actually his mother's evil, identical cousin! (Note: As if this story hasn't been crazy enough, why is there an identical cousin? Did the author think an evil identical twin was too cliche? She was right!) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Okay, one last thing, and this is just a laugh; maybe the author even did this on purpose. Several times she uses the word "busted" to mean "broke" (as in, "he busted the door down"). This was a little jarring every time, as I don't think this is a correct use of the word. But the last time she used it was really funny - one character in the book is an art collector, and one day he goes missing. The hero goes over to his house, and he finds everything a shambles, "the paintings slashed, the statuary busted." Was that an intentional joke? If so, good for her.<br /><br />Okay, seriously, this is the last thing, a little gem:<br /><br /><i>Blind rage clouded his vision, but he knew better than to show it. Disregarding his parents, he grabbed Julian by his dinner jacket and hurled him across the nearest table.</i><br /><br />Good thing he didn't let his anger show!<br /><br />Disclaimer: This is the second time I've posted a review for a book I listened to rather than read. Usually I don't review audiobooks because I feel like I haven't given the book a fair chance with my undivided attention. This book, however, doesn't deserve anyone's undivided attention, and I'm very confident this review wouldn't be any nicer if I had read the print version.<br /><br />If you enjoyed this review, check out <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2367657123?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">this review</a> of Some Girls Bite, a vampire novel of similar quality.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2756148782423665974" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_103312884" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/103312884" />
    <a title="Catherine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3282244-catherine"><img alt="Catherine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1277923282p2/3282244.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/103312884?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catherine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catherine" href="/user/show/3282244-catherine">Catherine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3282244-catherine?shelf=read-2010">read-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3282244-catherine?shelf=fantasy-paranormal-sci-fi">fantasy-paranormal-sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3282244-catherine?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3282244-catherine?shelf=aliens">aliens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3282244-catherine?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3282244-catherine?shelf=sucked">sucked</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3282244-catherine?shelf=assassin-killer-bounty-hunter">assassin-killer-bounty-hunter</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3282244-catherine?shelf=futuristic">futuristic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer103312884&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer103312884" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16254790288995193491">This book did not start off well for me. The author has a really bad habit of over describing <i>everything</i>. Every reference to something was like it was the first time. We had to hear the exact description all over again. Also, I really, <b>really</b> hate when an author has a character think something then immediately qualifies it. Like: <i>he didn't have time to humor her, but he ached so badly inside with the need to comfort her</i>. That was my own example, but crap like that happened constantly. Also, Nyky</span>
  <span id="freeText16254790288995193491" style="display:none">This book did not start off well for me. The author has a really bad habit of over describing <i>everything</i>. Every reference to something was like it was the first time. We had to hear the exact description all over again. Also, I really, <b>really</b> hate when an author has a character think something then immediately qualifies it. Like: <i>he didn't have time to humor her, but he ached so badly inside with the need to comfort her</i>. That was my own example, but crap like that happened constantly. Also, Nykyrian and Kiara did nothing but run around <i>aching</i>. Every time I turned a page Kiara was aching to kiss him again (while she hated him). It was ridiculous.<br /><br />Let's talk about Kiara. I disliked her for the first 100 pages and absolutely <i>hated</i> her for the next 200. I'm serious, I have never before loathed a character I was reading about. If I could have reached through the book to take her out of my misery I would have. She was such a rhymes-with-witch. Nykyrian and his crew get hired to protect her from the multitude of assassins after her. How does she respond to this? She whines. <i>Oh no, don't put better security on my home. I liked it how it was! Take your stupid blast shields and leave me here to die.</i> She was like that about everything.<br /><br />People constantly referred to her by her status, Princess. That's exactly what she was. A spoiled, snotty, self absorbed princess. When Syn finally saw her true attitude and blasted her for it I just wanted to give him a big smooch at how someone <i>finally</i> gave her the smack down and introduced her to reality. Unfortunately, she was too dumb and self absorbed to be moved by anything he said. <i>They're animals because they're not upset when they kill the people who are trying to kill her</i>. I mean seriously, what kind of idiot is this girl? These people want to <b>rape and kill you</b>! They've captured you more than once. But you're mad because Nykyrian killed them and saved you from them? She was so disgusted by him she threw up later. I have to stop talking about her, I'm getting mad all over again.<br /><br />Nykyrian was a typical hero by this author. He's huge and a bad ass and has a tortured childhood. If you've read a book by her you'll recognize him. I didn't really mind that part, but I did mind his relationship with Kiara. The situation reminded me of a stray dog who has been beaten often. He's frightening and apt to attack first rather than let anyone get close. But still that dog longs for someone to pet him. So, he meets this human. The human is mean to him too. But one day the human decides to take pity on him and feed him and love him. This dog is eventually so grateful that he gives her all his love and devotion and totally ignores any time she's mean to him. That's exactly how their relationship was. To my eyes anyone would have done. He caved at the first hint of basic human kindness. It was sad, not sexy.<br /><br />By the way, when Kiara's so called "turning" point came about she was watching private movies of his childhood. No explanation was ever given for why any of these things were ever recorded and how he got ahold of them. These were not regular movies. They were recordings of him being beaten at home, at school, and one of his first meeting with Syn out on the street where no one else was. So, where did these movies come from? It makes no sense and was rather weak. So, seeing these movies "changes" Kiara. He's pissed at her (rightfully so) for watching his movies, but two seconds later they're making out. Their sex life takes off from there.<br /><br />After that point in the book it's like we're reading about a whole new character. She's still irritating, but now she's sickly sweet too. I seriously wouldn't have been surprised if she had grabbed his cheeks and rubbed noses with him while calling him snookums. Blech. So they continue their relationship until <b>the big misunderstanding</b>. The end comes pretty quickly after that with a pretty lame reveal about Nykyrian's past. Thank God that came along out of nowhere to help you have a future with Kiara.<br /><br />The last 200ish pages were 3 stars for me, just average. I didn't hate it, but I didn't like it either. The first 300ish pages were a 1 star for me. Kiara made me loathe them. So I averaged it out to a 2 star. <br /><br /><b>Edited to add</b>: I can't believe I forgot to rant about something that drove me nuts in the book! Kiara and her forgiveness of her father. Nykyrian takes Kiara back to see her dad and her dad orders him killed right there in front of her! She throws herself to the ground and "wails" until her dad comes and carries her away. She's cold to him for months, but she still stays in his home. Then when she finds out that Nykyrian isn't really dead she stops being mad at her dad entirely. <b>The intent was still there! Just because it didn't succeed doesn't mean he should be forgiven. He never even apologized. He wanted to make her get rid of the baby so she could get back to dancing. He was a jerk! </b></span>
  <a data-text-id="16254790288995193491" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_81686496" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/81686496" />
    <a title="Shawna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1802746-shawna"><img alt="Shawna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574172018p2/1802746.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/81686496?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shawna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shawna" href="/user/show/1802746-shawna">Shawna</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of paranormal romance &amp; tortured heroes</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Shawna by: </span>
      Shana
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=hero-addict-excon-lawtrouble-thief">hero-addict-excon-lawtrouble-thief</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=hero-recluse-loner-lonewolf">hero-recluse-loner-lonewolf</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer81686496" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9163835828459405854">5 stars – Paranormal/Sci-Fi Romance<br/><br/>I’ve had Kenyon’s <i>Dark-Hunter</i> series on my TBR list for quite some time now, but I’m a little bit intimated by the number of books there are to get caught up on. The premise of <i>The League</i> series sounded interesting, the characters seemed intriguing, and with only three books produced so far, it felt a little less daunting of an undertaking. The main word that comes to mind to describe how I felt about this book is...WOW! And if it’s indicative of her other work</span>
  <span id="freeText9163835828459405854" style="display:none">5 stars – Paranormal/Sci-Fi Romance<br /><br />I’ve had Kenyon’s <i>Dark-Hunter</i> series on my TBR list for quite some time now, but I’m a little bit intimated by the number of books there are to get caught up on. The premise of <i>The League</i> series sounded interesting, the characters seemed intriguing, and with only three books produced so far, it felt a little less daunting of an undertaking. The main word that comes to mind to describe how I felt about this book is...WOW! And if it’s indicative of her other works, then I can certainly understand why Kenyon’s <i>Dark-Hunter</i> series is so popular and has such a large fan following.<br /><br />The Ichidian Universe that SK has created in <i>The League</i> series is unique and fascinating, and I never felt overwhelmed, confused, or bored at all by the world-building...just completely immersed and entertained. And oh my...Assassin Nykyrian is so sexy, mysterious, captivating, and complex, and he’s one of the darkest, most tortured romantic heroes ever. Seriously, he’s right up there with Judd from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/458034.Caressed_By_Ice__Psy_Changeling___3_" title="Caressed By Ice (Psy-Changeling, #3) by Nalini Singh" rel="nofollow noopener">Caressed By Ice</a>, Dante from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2081569.A_Rush_of_Wings__The_Maker_s_Song___1_" title="A Rush of Wings (The Maker's Song, #1) by Adrian Phoenix" rel="nofollow noopener">A Rush of Wings</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2888973.In_the_Blood__The_Maker_s_Song___2_" title="In the Blood (The Maker's Song, #2) by Adrian Phoenix" rel="nofollow noopener">In the Blood</a>, and Reyes from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2712967.The_Darkest_Pleasure__Lords_of_the_Underworld___3_" title="The Darkest Pleasure (Lords of the Underworld, #3) by Gena Showalter" rel="nofollow noopener">The Darkest Pleasure</a> for the best anguished, tarnished hero (although no one can top my beloved Zsadist from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/42900.Lover_Awakened__Black_Dagger_Brotherhood___3_" title="Lover Awakened (Black Dagger Brotherhood, #3) by J.R. Ward" rel="nofollow noopener">Lover Awakened</a>). Nyk’s past is so sad and brutally painful, that it actually brought tears to my eyes, and the romance between him and Kiara is intense, touching, at times heartbreaking, and very hot.<br /><br /><b>Born of Night</b> is an amazing paranormal romance, and I’m looking forward to more in this awesome series...and hopefully to finally reading the <i>Dark-Hunter</i> books at some point in the future, too! Big 5 stars!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9163835828459405854" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_103933513" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/103933513" />
    <a title="UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish"><img alt="UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1398981306p2/1113032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/103933513?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish" href="/user/show/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish">UniquelyMoi ~ BlithelyBookish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Light Sci-Fi fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=abuse-physical-emotional-sexual">abuse-physical-emotional-sexual</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=author-sherrilyn-kenyon">author-sherrilyn-kenyon</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=own-have-read">own-have-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=2010-reads">2010-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1113032-uniquelymoi-blithelybookish?shelf=reviewed-by-me">reviewed-by-me</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer103933513" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17751502332060111807"><br/>I’ve been a huge fan of Sherrilyn Kenyon’s writing ever since I first discovered the Dark-Hunter series and that amazing hero, Acheron. When I heard about the re-release of The League series, I was thrilled until I learned it was Sci-Fi because I’m really not a big fan of the genre. Truthfully, the only other Sci-Fi book I have ever read and really liked, <i>loved</i> in fact, was <i>The Host</i> by Stephenie Meyer. <i>The Host,</i> like <i>Born of Night </i> was pretty light on the techie stuff which is why it worked for </span>
  <span id="freeText17751502332060111807" style="display:none"><br />I’ve been a huge fan of Sherrilyn Kenyon’s writing ever since I first discovered the Dark-Hunter series and that amazing hero, Acheron. When I heard about the re-release of The League series, I was thrilled until I learned it was Sci-Fi because I’m really not a big fan of the genre. Truthfully, the only other Sci-Fi book I have ever read and really liked, <i>loved</i> in fact, was <i>The Host</i> by Stephenie Meyer. <i>The Host,</i> like <i>Born of Night </i> was pretty light on the techie stuff which is why it worked for me. The time period, the locations and everyday living were given enough attention to detail that there was no mistaking the book’s futuristic setting, yet at the same time I didn’t feel like I needed a degree in rocket science to understand what was happening. And while this has nothing to do with the genre, in the beginning there were so many characters being introduced, relationships explained and back-stories given, that I wasn’t sure I’d ever be able to fully follow the story. However once I got into the book and became familiar with the names, I had no problem whatsoever. <br /><br />Keeping in mind that this was Sherrilyn Kenyon’s debut novel, something minor I want to mention is that I know that sometimes when we buy a book for the author’s name, we expect it to be at least as good as their last book we read. I ran into this recently when I began reading some books that were written by one of my all time favorite authors, J.R. Ward, writing as Jessica Bird. The Bird books were excellent, but didn’t have the same “feel” or “flawless flow” as the Ward books do and while <i>Born of Night</i> is a great story, I could see a slight difference in the writing refinement. I’m truly not trying to be critical, merely pointing this out for readers who may not be aware that these books were written years before her Dark-Hunter series was released and might wonder about the difference in writing.<br /><br />However, all that said, I’m very impressed by how well written this debut novel is. The plot is believable, the characters well defined and with a depth of moral character that I couldn’t help but be proud of these "criminals" who are consider to be low life scum by the “important” people, the ones who supposedly matter.<br /><br />Overall, I really enjoyed this book and adored Nykerian! As for Kiara - <i>meh</i> - she was annoying as all get out and I really didn’t see how I’d ever come to like her enough to want to see Nyk saddled with her for the rest of his life. Indeed, oft was the time that I silently urged Nykie to put her rear end on the first asteroid out of the galaxy, however, as only an author of Ms. Kenyon’s caliber can do, she took the irritating traits, flaws and weaknesses inherent in Kiara and explained them all so well that in the end, I had found it in my heart to forgive her and yes, even like her, and was very happy with the match.<br /><br />If you find yourself tempted, yet hesitant to read this book because it’s Sci-Fi, I’d really encourage you to take the chance. What have you got to lose?<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17751502332060111807" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer300409255" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13427861124193774674"><b>Final rating: 5/5 stars</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“If I have to die, I’d rather die knowing someone cared about me, just once. Is that really too much to ask?"<br/>"For us? Yes. It is. We are the gutter and the gutter is all we’ll ever be. Don’t reach out for the stars. They’ll burn you until there’s nothing left. "<br/>"Then let me burn.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><b>Reread this because i needed to remind myself how much i love this series </b>(i actually read all of the books and i am quite up to date with them, but i need to love them again). Not to</span>
  <span id="freeText13427861124193774674" style="display:none"><b>Final rating: 5/5 stars</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“If I have to die, I’d rather die knowing someone cared about me, just once. Is that really too much to ask?"<br>"For us? Yes. It is. We are the gutter and the gutter is all we’ll ever be. Don’t reach out for the stars. They’ll burn you until there’s nothing left. "<br>"Then let me burn.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><b>Reread this because i needed to remind myself how much i love this series </b>(i actually read all of the books and i am quite up to date with them, but i need to love them again). Not to mention how much i love all characters in it, especially Nykyrian, Syn and Darling &amp; Maris ♥. I also cried again, little less then i cried the first time, but i also laughed like crazy woman on all those hilarious moments.<b> My love for this series is huge, the characters are unforgettable, and it's the ability of Sherrilyn Kenyon to make them so loveable. I seriously love you woman! </b><br><br>Oh, and one more thing! The author herself said that there were two versions of this book. The earlier one, which has "the" in the title...aka "Born of THE night", and it's different, so i suggest you search for this one (there is a short author's note on the beginning, saying the version is new one).<br>____________________________________________<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <u>WORLD BUILDING AND THE STORY</u>
  </i>
</b>: <br>____________________________________________<br><br>Sooooooo....let me start with the introduction to the world. <br><br>♦ There is <b>the League.</b> They are assassins and they are cruel, vicious and sometimes horrible. They are legendary, they are unstoppable, and they are some kind of law. <br><br>♦ <b>The Sentella </b> on the other hand is a organization made to keep the League in the check - but they are all criminals and they are crazy. In a positive way, btw. It's an organization that has the same reason for existing as the League does and that is to protect people from those who are corrupted by power. <br><br>♦ <b> Andarions </b> are the race who genetically come from humans, but they refuse to acknowledge it. They are fierce, they are vicious, and are predatorial race that sometimes fed on humans. They are long fanged, have red rimmed eyes, and they always have black hair. And they are scary as hell to regular people.They also value physical beauty only second to physical strength. <br><br>♦ There are also<b> many planetary systems</b>, some of them are populated with humans and are empires and such. For example,there exists Caron, a human system, and so on and on....<br><br><b> The story </b> on the other hand is about Nykyrian, a former League assassin - he left the League a long time ago, and they still haven't killed him - because he kills them first. He is a member of Sentella. <br><br>And then, one day, Sentella goes on a mission and Syn, one of them, finds Kiara and rescues her. Together with Nykyrian who is in disguise as Nemesis, the scarriest, the most brutal assassin Sentella has. <br><br>After they rescued her, Sentella signed up to be bodyguards for Kiara until the danger on her life passes...<br>____________________________________________<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <u>CHARACTERS</u>
  </i>
</b>: <br>____________________________________________<br><br>♦ <b>
  <i>
    <u>Nykyrian:</u>
  </i>
</b><br><br>Nykyrian...Oh Nykyrian... He is a hybrid of two races - he is half human and half Andarion. They are extremely rare, but the problem lies in the fact that Andarions think he is weak and therefore is an outcast, and humans fear him because they think he would eat them and therefore he had been outcasted again. If only it was an easy thing. He once had family, he had status, he had everything, until the day when he was a just a child, when he lost everything - and from that moment on, his life had been nothing but utter and complete misery, terror and suffering. He was trained to be the most vicious, the most lethal, emotionless assassin, until one day he decided it was enough and escaped. And then, he joined Sentella and became one of the most feared assassins, called Nemesis. But even he has a heart, and he has emotions, and deep inside, he is afraid of showing anything, lest he suffers rejection again. He never smiles, he is quite sarcastic and he is sometimes ironic as hell.<br><br>And then...he meets Kiara, who changes his perspective on the world...or not. She also many many times misunderstands him, and therefore, she hurts him again, and again and again. But he couldn't help eventually falling in love with her (which took half of the book) and he decided that he could change...for her. But, he doesn't trust easily, he doesn't open easily and he certainly doesn't feel like he needs someone. He is so much used thinking that he was alone, that he doesn't see the truth; people care about him, Sentella members especially, but he doesn't notice it.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> “In your palms, I’ve placed my life, my secrets. I give you freedom to leave me at any time. I’m not easy to love. No one ever has. All I ask is that you always keep your silence, if not for me, then for the families of the others you’d destroy.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Reading about his past always destroys me. I seriously wonder how he stayed sane through it all and how he turned out to be a seriously wonderful, gentle and sane person... It's a wonder. <br><br>♦ <b>
  <i>
    <u>Kiara:</u>
  </i>
</b><br><br>Kiara has everything - she is rich, spoiled, she has normal family, she is loved, she is famous, she is a dancer. But then again, is she good human being? Yes. She is, though sometimes she can be utter and horrible bitch (still i don't blame her). She doesn't think about the things she says, she thinks she knows it all, and she is quick to judge. I wanted to strangle her - and i wonder how Syn didn't do it already xD<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Everyone has a choice. (Kiara)<br>No, princess, they don’t. Choices aren’t always up to us. Life and circumstances can shred even the stoutest soul. No matter how pure and untainted you think you are, I promise you that you, too, can be shoved into the darkness, just like we were. (Syn)” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>But, then again, she is wonderful, she is nice and she is total match for Nykyrian. She falls in love with him slowly, especially after she slowly cracks his shell... She finds out that life can be a bitch, that not everyone lived the same way as she did and it made her understand how happy she actually was and is in her life and in her skin.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b> “I wish I could take away your pain. I wish I could go back to when you were born and take you somewhere safe. Far away from all the people who’ve hurt you.”<br>His eyes were liquid emeralds. “You’re doing that now.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>♦ <b>
  <i>
    <u>Sentella members:</u>
  </i>
</b><br><br>The Sentella memebers are unique. They are all criminals, that is true. But - they are good - they are never bad and they have never been bad, but it doesn't make them less criminal. Everyone judges them before they even met them, and all of them hide some deep and traumatic pasts (not sure about Hauk though). They are batshit insane and crazy and funny as hell. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“What the hell was that action?” Syn asked him.<br>“I think it’s something called ‘paternal concern.’ ”<br>Syn scowled at his bland explanation. “What . . . ? You sure? I thought that crap was a myth.”<br>Nykyrian shrugged. “No, really. I watched it once in a documentary. It was fascinating. Believe it or not, there are people out there who actually have feelings for their progeny.”<br>“Get the fuck out. No way. You’re screwing with my head again, aren’t you?”<br>“No. I swear. You just saw it with your own eyes. I did not make that shit up.”<br>Syn shivered. “Yeah but it’s really messing with my concept of the natural order of the universe. Paternal love? What’s next? Limb regrowth? Genetic splicing reversals?”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Hauk is an Andarion, he is funny, scary and awesome (he is not interested in humans). Syn, one of my fav characters is crazy SOB who drinks himself almost everytime, not to mention that he considers Nyk his best friend, and he was always there for him. And his sense of humor is fascinating. Darling...oh god..Darling - i fell in love the moment i first read about him. He is a redhead(yes i had to say it), he is scarred, and he is...well...just fantastic (especially after you read his book). I always hated his situation with his family, and it hurt me every time :(( <br><br>♦ <b>
  <i>
    <u>Other characters:</u>
  </i>
</b><br><br>All of the families in this series are insane! We have some overprotective fathers, dead mothers, dead sisters and unknown daughters, ignorant parents, psychotic brothers and lots and lots of killers. Well, let's just say, there is a long list of people/charaters i wanted to slaughter. <br><br>____________________________________________<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <u>OVERALL</u>
  </i>
</b>: <br>____________________________________________<br><br><b> Anyway...I fell in love with the dancer and the assassin. Just reading the synopsis for the first time grabbed my attention + it was Sherri, so could i ask for more? I think i love this series more than i love her Dark Hunters. And also, her ability to produce tortured heroes is amazing (even heroines). If you like science fiction, with good world building, romance, action and hotness, and if you love tortured heroes and great characters, than this series must be read.</b><br><br>The rest of the league books...Bring it on!!!<br>____________________________________________<br><br>● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ● ●<br>____________________________________________ <br><br><b> MY THE LEAGUE REVIEWS: </b><br><br> ◉ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/300409255" rel="nofollow noopener"> Born of Night (The League, #1) </a><br> ◉ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/380403154" rel="nofollow noopener"> Cloak &amp; Silence (The League, #7) </a><br> ◉ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/300409401" rel="nofollow noopener"> Born of Fury (The League, #8) </a><br> ◉ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1067505905" rel="nofollow noopener"> Born of Defiance (The League, #9) </a><br> ◉ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1067505849" rel="nofollow noopener"> Born of Betrayal (The League, #10) </a><br><br><br><b>
  <i><br>This review can be found on my blog: <a href="http://infinity-of-time.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">infinity-of-time.blogspot.com</a> also known as... </i>
</b><br><a href="http://infinity-of-time.blogspot.com/2013/04/born-of-night-league-1-by-sherrilyn.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380363317i/714576.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1519631539" />
    <a title="Jo ★The Book Sloth★" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13870608-jo-the-book-sloth"><img alt="Jo ★The Book Sloth★" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487525094p2/13870608.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1519631539?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo ★The Book Sloth★" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo ★The Book Sloth★" href="/user/show/13870608-jo-the-book-sloth">Jo ★The Book Sloth★</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13870608-jo-the-book-sloth?shelf=insta-love-lust">insta-love-lust</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13870608-jo-the-book-sloth?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13870608-jo-the-book-sloth?shelf=like-a-virgin">like-a-virgin</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13870608-jo-the-book-sloth?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13870608-jo-the-book-sloth?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13870608-jo-the-book-sloth?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1519631539" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2073730868793142894"><b>5 Stars</b> <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455371438i/18094047.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>Nykyrian Quikiades is the man behind the Nemesis mask, a name that strikes fear to the hearts of the most hardened criminals. A fugitive from the League, with contracts for his assassination from several planets goverments, Nykyrian is a man fighting a war against an organisation that has grown too corrupt to dispense the justice and protection it was founded for. His latest responsibility is protecting Princess Kiara Zamir, a woman caught in the middle of her father's political differen</i></span>
  <span id="freeText2073730868793142894" style="display:none"><b>5 Stars</b> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455371438i/18094047.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Nykyrian Quikiades is the man behind the Nemesis mask, a name that strikes fear to the hearts of the most hardened criminals. A fugitive from the League, with contracts for his assassination from several planets goverments, Nykyrian is a man fighting a war against an organisation that has grown too corrupt to dispense the justice and protection it was founded for. His latest responsibility is protecting Princess Kiara Zamir, a woman caught in the middle of her father's political differences with his enemies.<br><br>Kiara Zamir is no stranger to fear. She felt it to the bone when she was eight and watched her mother die on the hands of their kidnappers. Now the terror of running for her life is back by the target painted on her back but at least this time she has Nykyrian and the Sentella looking out for her. Nykyrian with the tortured eyes and the air of mystery that attract her as much as his assassin job repells her. Can she get over her aversion to violence to see the man behind the mask?</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455371811i/18094187.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>From one of my favorite Paranormal authors a series that's par Sci-fi, part Paranormal and all Action and Romance. Once again Sherrilyn Kenyon managed to suck me right in with her complex plotlines and multi-dimensional characters. She made me laugh and cry and sympathise with everything they went through. She made me want to learn more about them and their world. I'm not going to review every book in the series(because I'm sooo not reviewing 10 books right now) but I will say that much like her Dark Hunter series there is one constant in every book. <b>Sherrilyn Kenyon sure loves to torture her heroes!</b> She puts them through hell and in the end rewards them with what they want most for all the pain they've suffered. She also makes them resilient(some even immortal) just so she can torture them some more. AND I LOVE EVERY MINUTE OF IT!<br><br>Born Of Night is no exception to the rule. What Nykyrian has been through had me to tears more than once. The stuff he had to do to survive, the pain he had to suffer, the sheer strength of will it took to get through the hell other people's prejudice put him through, made me ache and root for him from start to finish. His badass attitude and hotness didn't hurt either. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455372342i/18094262.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Kiara was also no delicate flower. Despite the fact that she spent most of her life protected in the cocoon her father had surrounded her with, she had met her fair share of pain. She wasn't blind to the cruelty people were capable of, even though she may not have exactly been aware of the extend people could go to to hurt other people. I liked her backbone and her determination to not be a victim for anyone.<br><br>I also loved the world SK has created. Although ten books later I still have plenty of questions regarding how things work in the Universe she has created. Still, the intergalactic travels, the advanced weaponry, the out-there technology and the different forms of civilization are enough to keep this girl glued to the pages of each and every book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2073730868793142894" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1283629794" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1283629794" />
    <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin"><img alt="Mike (the Paladin)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528431476p2/2187043.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1283629794?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike (the Paladin)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike (the Paladin)" href="/user/show/2187043-mike-the-paladin">Mike (the Paladin)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2187043-mike-the-paladin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1283629794" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3258199748225680861">I thought I might like this one. It opened with an intro to our anti-hero as he refused to kill a child in his role as exceptionally deadly assassin. He contacts a friend who it seems might be telling the story and takes his leave so as to protect said friend. He's going to fight rather than be killed by his former superiors...the only outcome for an assassin who wants to, "retire".<br/><br/>Then we jump to the point of view of a scrappy young woman who's been kidnapped. She fights against her situation, </span>
  <span id="freeText3258199748225680861" style="display:none">I thought I might like this one. It opened with an intro to our anti-hero as he refused to kill a child in his role as exceptionally deadly assassin. He contacts a friend who it seems might be telling the story and takes his leave so as to protect said friend. He's going to fight rather than be killed by his former superiors...the only outcome for an assassin who wants to, "retire".<br /><br />Then we jump to the point of view of a scrappy young woman who's been kidnapped. She fights against her situation, she will not give up, she'll die first. Then the ship (that's a space ship) in which she's being held comes under attack. Well she thinks, that's it I'll die here. Then against all hope she's rescued...by the universe's most feared (and possibly hated) assassin. She thinks almost hateful thoughts about him....<br /><br />And then the book goes completely off the rails. From this point on neither character (victim or assassin) think of anything except their lust, love, obsession and desire for the other. Sweating, panting and over-heated the girl who was just rescued from certain death can't look at the guy (whom up till now she'd hated on principal from reputation alone) without losing it completely and falling into sexual fantasy. The hard, cold, viscous assassin whom no one has ever survived goes "hard" (the book's description not mine) at the very thought of the girl. <br /><br /><i>Excuse me while I stifle my gag reflex, roll my eyes and sigh deeply.</i>.<br /><br />Look I can take a love story, I can take some romance...but I don't like books that are romances. If that's the point of the book, don't call it action. Don't give a synopsis about a galaxy class assassin and daring do if the books pages are going to be filled with adolescent lust fantasies.<br /><br />So, don't care for it-can't recommend it. if you want a romance try this one. If you want an action read about a reforming assassin maybe not. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3258199748225680861" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_57652269" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/57652269" />
    <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"><img alt=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403239075p2/1570669.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/57652269?book_show_action=true">May 28, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"> Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of futuristic/sci-fi romance and action, Sherrilyn Kenyon fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=knight-in-tarnished-armor">knight-in-tarnished-armor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=favorite-or-autobuy-author">favorite-or-autobuy-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=owned-copy">owned-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=hero-to-die-for">hero-to-die-for</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=bodyguard-protector">bodyguard-protector</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=futuristic">futuristic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=space-another-planet">space-another-planet</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer57652269" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16044028250574266153">Okay, I think I am an official futuristic/space romance convert now. I loved what Ms. Kenyon did with this concept. I thought she did a very good job with the world-building, but I caught a couple of 'slips' where she would describe things that I really had trouble believing they would have in a futuristic setting on another planet. But then I have no creativity when it comes to making up technological devices and futuristic settings, so I can hardly judge her. Overall, I was happy and I didn't </span>
  <span id="freeText16044028250574266153" style="display:none">Okay, I think I am an official futuristic/space romance convert now. I loved what Ms. Kenyon did with this concept. I thought she did a very good job with the world-building, but I caught a couple of 'slips' where she would describe things that I really had trouble believing they would have in a futuristic setting on another planet. But then I have no creativity when it comes to making up technological devices and futuristic settings, so I can hardly judge her. Overall, I was happy and I didn't find those rare instances jarring. I think she did a great job coming up with the different cultures and races. It wasn't to the degree that I got bored, and neither was the technological references. I don't like my sci-fi to be top heavy with this kind of stuff. Just enough to make me believe the setting, thanks very much. <br /><br />Some of the aspects with the League of Assassins Academy and the political structure aspects reminded me vaguely of Star Trek, but this book is not very much in that vein at all. If anything it is more like Firefly. Sigh. Yes, I definitely had happy reminders of the short-lived but brilliant show Firefly with this book. The characters aren't that similar but some of the aspects of the universe and the social/political structures are. There is the whole fancy politically-structured universe paired to the backwater planets theme that is prevalent in the Firefly universe. Also the group of smugglers and outlaws that Nykyrian associates with reminds me of heavily of the crew and passengers of Serenity, and some of the folks they encounter in the various episodes. That's where the similarity ends, because this story is Classic Sherrilyn Kenyon. Sorry, Malcolm Reynolds lovers. There is no Mal character in this book. But we have Nykyrian, and he rules this book. <br /> <br /><br />A newbie to tortured heroes? Meet Nykyrian Quikiades. This man takes the cake for this hero archetype. Was that a bad thing for this reader? Certainly not. I love tortured heroes. Nykyrian earns his spot on my hero to die for list. I found myself rooting for him, crushing on him, and almost crying for him, and deeply feeling for him. That's a good sign.<br /><br />And Ms. Kenyon reaffirms to me why I love her books with this novel. She writes romance novels that read like my favorite action/adventure movies (with the amped up romance that is usually missing from some of my cinematic fare of my choice). I know I talk about movies a lot when I review books. I can't help it. I am a Movie Buff and a Bookworm. Those areas often overlap for me. Anyhoo, there is a bit of Cleric John Preston in fair Nykyrian. Oh, yes. That is a good thing, since Cleric John Preston from Equilibrium is a Certified, Grade A Badass. So is Nykyrian. He is absolutely lethal and he doesn't have to concentrate to be that way. His lethality is actually hard for Kiara to deal with after he goes futuristic/medieval on some badguys who were trying to kill her. I had a little bit of a "I want to slap the heroine of this book really hard" moment when she treats him like garbage afterwords. I told myself to calm down and remember what she went through. She had been kidnapped and was tortured, had to watch her mother be tortured and killed, was almost murdered herself, and had survived several other attempts on her life. I could understand her dislike of violent people. However, there are some instances where violence is the answer for other violence. In other words, she lives in a shades of gray universe, not a black and white one. She should have been more conscious of that before she started condemning Nyk and his colleagues. There are many instances of violence towards her and the other characters, that really did demand a response in kind.<br /><br />I was really glad that Nykyrian's friend Syn told her off. She needed to hear that because she had badly misjudged Nyk. I a not a fan of cruel bullies and conscienceless murderers (despite my love of antiheroes and assassins). It was clear to me early own that this was so not Nykyrian. I think that Kiara really needed a reality check on Nyk. She has a couple of moments where she shows some emotional immaturity that irked me, but overall, she really comes through for Nyk. So I guess she can have him (even though I want him all to myself). <br /><br />He's got so much damage and pain in his past, present, and future. Ms. Kenyon says in the introduction that she added back the parts that the publisher would not allow in the first publication since they were too intense. Yup, they were intense. She definitely didn't pull her punches with this one. I haven't read Acheron yet, so I don't know if Ash had it worse, but gosh I don't know if I'll be able to stand it if he did. Nykyrian really had a crap life. Some really awful things happen to him, so the reader should be warned that some of this is not pretty at all. But it really helped me to understand the person that he is. No wonder he doesn't trust anyone and is cold, isolated, and lethal, or maintains a facade to this effect. <br /><br />Kiara was a good heroine. She had her moments where she annoyed me, but she turns out to be the right woman for Nyk. Ms. Kenyon doesn't seem to do tormented heroines, and Kiara isn't exactly one. But she's had some bad stuff happen in her past that flavors her and gives her added depth. I liked the aspects of her career as a dancer. I think Ms. Kenyon must have known a dancer or have been a dancer, because this felt very authentic.<br /><br />The love scenes are very light, so don't read this expecting a lot of steam. But I didn't mind that at all. I liked them, because they showed the tenderness and the connection between Nykyrian and Kiara.<br /><br />I'm loving Nyk's friends and sidekicks. They were all very interesting, adding to the flavor of this book. The dialog between them was great. Kenyon certainly knows how to turn on the snark and to have you laughing. My favorite secondary character was Syn. I'm excited to read Syn's story. He's funny and interesting, and he's got a lot of anguish that should make for an interesting journey in his novel. I also really liked Darling. I hope he gets his happy ending (although it wouldn't be the traditional boy/girl kind of romance).<br /><br />I don't want to give spoilers, but readers will find that Nyk's past intersects very heavily with his future, giving him closure and opens a door for new beginnings. I must say I enjoyed that aspect of this story.<br /><br />I'm very glad that this League series came back into print. I love the setting and the characters, and it meets my sci-fi-loving needs, with some great romance and action in a wonderful combination. I look forward to reading the rest of the books in the series. <br /><br />FYI: The short story in the Man of My Dreams anthology is about Nykyrian and Kiara's son. It's awesome.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16044028250574266153" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6962062509401538685">This was simply amazing. I thought I would get tired by its size, but as it turned out, I wasn't bored for a single minute while reading this. Fans of tortured heroes who also happen to be mercenaries/assasins/outlaws should grab this one asap as Nykyrian is one of the best heroes in that area. Think about Zarek or Judd Laurens or Bastien. <br/><br/>The last 100 pages disappointed me somewhat with the way the plot twisted in so many ways, but in the end, nothing can dull the awesomeness of this book. Happ</span>
  <span id="freeText6962062509401538685" style="display:none">This was simply amazing. I thought I would get tired by its size, but as it turned out, I wasn't bored for a single minute while reading this. Fans of tortured heroes who also happen to be mercenaries/assasins/outlaws should grab this one asap as Nykyrian is one of the best heroes in that area. Think about Zarek or Judd Laurens or Bastien. <br /><br />The last 100 pages disappointed me somewhat with the way the plot twisted in so many ways, but in the end, nothing can dull the awesomeness of this book. Happily continuing with the next in the series, Syn's story.<br /><br />Warning: the book is sci-fi and the hero is not human, although he is basically human in appearance. I'm not at all a fan of sci-fi romance, but in this case, it didn't bother me in the least. It was mostly like those PNR books set in the future where a few impressive gadgets are introduced but most things are familiar nonetheless.</span>

<div id="review_1428127951" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5252054-irena?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5252054-irena?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1428127951" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17283295233218210989"><b>2.5</b><br/><br/>I wish I'd read this when it was first published (and I hadn't been paying attention to certain things). I would have liked it more than I do now. <br/><br/>With that out of the way, if you aren't in the mood for a sci-fi paranormal romance featuring a very tortured hero and one of the most annoying heroines ever, I suggest you skip this. Since I was, you could say I kind of liked it. The first half of the story at least.<br/> I like this idea of the Ichidian Universe, where a small group of former assassin</span>
  <span id="freeText17283295233218210989" style="display:none"><b>2.5</b><br /><br />I wish I'd read this when it was first published (and I hadn't been paying attention to certain things). I would have liked it more than I do now. <br /><br />With that out of the way, if you aren't in the mood for a sci-fi paranormal romance featuring a very tortured hero and one of the most annoying heroines ever, I suggest you skip this. Since I was, you could say I kind of liked it. The first half of the story at least.<br /> I like this idea of the Ichidian Universe, where a small group of former assassins and fugitives have to fight off other, worse groups of killers. Then you get a glimpse of different races, cultures living on The League from the series title is an organization some of the protagonists left and now they always have to look over their shoulder in case someone decides to fulfil the contract on their heads.<br />In any case, it's a first book in the series so it's quite possible that other books are better (or that they don't have a heroine this annoying). <br /> <br />I didn't mind Nykyrian being perfect at all. I found it refreshing after all the whining and flip-flipping the heroine was doing. I get that she is a total opposite, that she was sheltered and hasn't got a clue about anything really, but the <i>I care-I don't care-he is evil-he isn't a monster-come here-go away</i> juggling made my head hurt. <br />On the other hand, there were a couple of decent twists in the story.<br /><br />In any case, I liked it enough to continue with the series. To say the world is promising would be an understatement (reason for my rating).</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11573088863297140043">Fantasy-A-Thon: Read a debut fantasy or backlist title<br/><br/>Born of Night probably isn't a 3 Star read but 2 Stars seemed harsh. <br/><br/>Born of Night is book 1 in The League series. Sherrilyn Kenyon is most known for her Dark-Hunter series but in the authors note Kenyon informs us that Born of Night was actually one of the first books she ever wrote. She began writing this book all the way back in 1986 but it wasn't published until 1996. Eventually it went out of print but thanks to a deal with St. Martin's </span>
  <span id="freeText11573088863297140043" style="display:none">Fantasy-A-Thon: Read a debut fantasy or backlist title<br /><br />Born of Night probably isn't a 3 Star read but 2 Stars seemed harsh. <br /><br />Born of Night is book 1 in The League series. Sherrilyn Kenyon is most known for her Dark-Hunter series but in the authors note Kenyon informs us that Born of Night was actually one of the first books she ever wrote. She began writing this book all the way back in 1986 but it wasn't published until 1996. Eventually it went out of print but thanks to a deal with St. Martin's she was able to get this book back into circulation with rewritten scenes and a more expanded world. <br /><br />The League is a group of highly trained Andarion assassins. Nykyrian Quiakides once the deadliest of the League decided to leave but since the League is like the Mafia (the only way out is in a casket) he is now being hunted by his former employers. Now he lives as a sort of bounty hunter/assassin. His current mission is to protect beautiful ballet dancer Kiara Zamir from her father's political foes who want her dead. <br /><br />I think we all know what happens next! <br /><br />He saves her life, they fall in love, have hot sex and live happily ever after. That's not a spoiler its just what happens in all these sort of books. I have nothing against a predictable fantasy romance but at least don't make me wait until halfway through the book for the sex. Also how many times did Kiara need to be threatened with rape by her captors? It was a little much. <br /><br />Born of Night wasn't bad but it wasn't all that interesting either. I won't be continuing this series, I much prefer her Dark-Hunter series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11573088863297140043" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<span id="freeTextContainer8492781771582071513">4.5 Rating.<br/><br/>Short review.<br/><br/>Excellent plot, characters, chemistry, pacing and so much more. <br/><br/>Loved this tortured hero and beautiful princess love story.   <span id="freeText8492781771582071513" style="display:none">4.5 Rating.<br /><br />Short review.<br /><br />Excellent plot, characters, chemistry, pacing and so much more. <br /><br />Loved this tortured hero and beautiful princess love story. Nykrian the hero was incredible. My heart broke for him and all he endured in his younger years, just heart heartwrenching . He was everything I look for in a hero, alpha, brave, sweet and totally in love with the heroine, just about perfect. Kiara, the heroine was beautiful, sassy and irritating for about a quarter of the book but redeemed herself from that point forward by giving Nykrian everything and anything to win him and their HEA. Just a beautiful love story.<br /><br />Something just draws me when the hero's character is an Assassin (but a redeemable one, oxymoron here I know) and the heroine a beautiful Princess. Kind of a fair tail love story I'm always a sucker for. The story was well written with the fantasy world coming to life and being so real like to the reader and clear. The character growth and depth was fantastic and well done. Secondary characters are almost as important and well developed as the MC. Pacing was fantastic, did not drag or seem slow at anytime in the book. <br /><br />What a wonderful and beautiful ending and epilogue. Fantastic read and highly recommended. <br /></span>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of the Black Dagger Brotherhood</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=aliens">aliens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=sexy-science-fiction">sexy-science-fiction</a>,
